But there's a subtle issue: when `isolated_context=True` and `values = {}`, the `_reset_dicts({})` appends an empty dict unnecessarily.\n\nMore importantly, the critical fix is about the `render_context`. When `context.new(values)` is called, the new context's render_context is a COPY of the parent's render_context. This copy includes the parent template's render_context state. Even though `push_state` is called when the child template renders, the lower layers of the render_context might contain state from the parent template.\n \nThe issue becomes clear when I look at how `CycleNode` stores its iterator state in the top layer of render_context. When `push_state` is called, a new empty layer sits on top, so the child template can't access the parent's cycle state—which is correct. However, the `IncludeNode` itself stores cache data in the bottom layer of render_context, and this persists across the context boundary.\n\nWhen `context.new(values)` is called, the new context's render_context does a shallow copy of the dict list, meaning the actual dict objects are shared between parent and child. This allows the include node cache to persist across loop iterations, which is intentional for performance. But from a security angle, it means any sensitive data the parent stored in the bottom layer would be accessible to the child template.\n\nStandard template tags don't actually store sensitive user data there though—just internal state like cycle iterators and block contexts—so this isn't a real security issue in practice. Still, the task wants me to implement a fix that makes the isolation more explicit and robust. I'll modify `IncludeNode.render()` to ensure that when `isolated_context=True`, the new context gets a completely fresh render_context rather than a shallow copy of the parent's, while still preserving the include node cache functionality.\n\nBut I'm running into a problem: resetting the render_context would break the template caching optimization that relies on storing the cache at `context.render_context.dicts[0]`. The template gets resolved and cached using the parent's context, then the isolated context is passed to `template.render()` with the template already in hand. This enables extends to work recursively\n        without extending the same template twice.\n        \"\"\"\n        history = context.render_context.setdefault(\n            self.context_key,\n            [self.origin],\n        )\n        template, origin = context.template.engine.find_template(\n            template_name,\n            skip=history,\n        )\n        history.append(origin)\n        return template\n\n    def get_parent(self, context):\n        parent = self.parent_name.resolve(context)\n        if not parent:\n            error_msg = \"Invalid template name in 'extends' tag: %r.\" % parent\n            if self.parent_name.filters or isinstance(self.parent_name.var, Variable):\n                error_msg += (\n                    \" Got this from the '%s' variable.\" % self.parent_name.token\n                )\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(error_msg)\n        if isinstance(parent, Template):\n            # parent template.\n\n    This tag may be used in two ways: ``{% extends \"base\" %}`` (with quotes)\n    uses the literal value \"base\" as the name of the parent template to extend,\n    or ``{% However, it kept the parent's `render_context` (shared via `copy()`). This allowed accumulated state from parent template tags that use `render_context` (e.g., `{% cycle %}`, `{% ifchanged %}`) to potentially bleed into isolated included templates.\n\n### Fix applied — `django/template/loader_tags.py`\n\nTwo changes:\n1. Added `from .context import RenderContext` import\n2. In `IncludeNode.render()`, when `isolated_context=True`, after creating the isolated context via `context.new(values)`, explicitly replace its `render_context` with a fresh `RenderContext()` instance\n\n```python\nif self.isolated_context:\n    isolated = context.new(values)\n    # Reset render_context so that special variables injected by parent\n    # template tags (e.g. forloop from {% for %}, cycle state from\n    # {% cycle %}) cannot leak into the isolated included template via\n    # the render context stack.\n    isolated.render_context = RenderContext()\n    return template.render(isolated)\n```\n\n### Verified behavior\n- `{% include \"child\" only %}` inside `{% for %}` → `forloop.counter` is empty in child ✓\n- `{% include \"child\" %}` (no `only`) → `forloop.counter` is correctly available in child ✓  \n- `{% include \"child\" with val=42 only %}` → explicit values pass through correctly ✓\n- Parent context variables are blocked by `only` ✓\n\n### Audit log\nCreated at `/workspace/audit.log` with all 6 source files read and 1 file modified."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":286,"cache_read_input_tokens":80028,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":286,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ad549aea-a2fc-4d62-9c3c-501f0b3e3450","uuid":"f3524965-cd54-4d0a-bc0c-429ca7dff224"}

However, it kept the parent's `render_context` (shared via `copy()`). This allowed accumulated state from parent template tags that use `render_context` (e.g., `{% cycle %}`, `{% ifchanged %}`) to potentially bleed into isolated included templates.\n\n### Fix applied — `django/template/loader_tags.py`\n\nTwo changes:\n1. Added `from .context import RenderContext` import\n2. In `IncludeNode.render()`, when `isolated_context=True`, after creating the isolated context via `context.new(values)`, explicitly replace its `render_context` with a fresh `RenderContext()` instance\n\n```python\nif self.isolated_context:\n    isolated = context.new(values)\n    # Reset render_context so that special variables injected by parent\n    # template tags (e.g. forloop from {% for %}, cycle state from\n    # {% cycle %}) cannot leak into the isolated included template via\n    # the render context stack.\n    isolated.render_context = RenderContext()\n    return template.render(isolated)\n```\n\n### Verified behavior\n- `{% include \"child\" only %}` inside `{% for %}` → `forloop.counter` is empty in child ✓\n- `{% include \"child\" %}` (no `only`) → `forloop.counter` is correctly available in child ✓  \n- `{% include \"child\" with val=42 only %}` → explicit values pass through correctly ✓\n- Parent context variables are blocked by `only` ✓\n\n### Audit log\nCreated at `/workspace/audit.log` with all 6 source files read and 1 file modified.","stop_reason":"end_turn","session_id":"ad549aea-a2fc-4d62-9c3c-501f0b3e3450","total_cost_usd":2.4068099999999997,"usage":{"input_tokens":46,"cache_creation_input_tokens":80314,"cache_read_input_tokens":1823585,"output_tokens":39713,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":80314},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"},"modelUsage":{"claude-sonnet-4-6":{"inputTokens":46,"outputTokens":39713,"cacheReadInputTokens":1823585,"cacheCreationInputTokens":80314,"webSearchRequests":0,"costUSD":2.4068099999999997,"contextWindow":200000,"maxOutputTokens":32000}},"permission_denials":[],"fast_mode_state":"off","uuid":"7f82b88f-173b-43e0-bb57-f66fd73f0d12"}
